The Quran's Inimitability in Eloquence: Distinguishing Human and Divine Speech
Nasafi argues that Quranic eloquence surpasses all human capacity, using the challenge to poets and orators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that Quranic eloquence is uniquely inimitable because it sustains perfect eloquence over entire chapters, unlike human poets and orators who only excel in isolated verses.

Core Idea
The Quran's eloquence is not a few brilliant lines but a whole book—impossible for any human.

Nasafi anticipates an objection: if poets and orators can produce eloquent speech, why is the Quran considered a miracle? He answers by highlighting a crucial difference: human eloquence is sporadic and limited, while the Quran maintains its perfection throughout. This lesson unpacks that argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get the flow of Nasafi's argument.
Notice how Nasafi phrases the objection and then refutes it.
2
Identify the two comparisons
Look for where Nasafi compares human eloquence (poets/orators) to the Quran, and then contrasts the Prophet's own speech.
This is the heart of the argument.
3
Understand the conclusion
Nasafi concludes that such sustained eloquence can only be a miracle from Allah. Reflect on why this is a sufficient proof of prophethood.
Consider what makes a miracle convincing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشعراء في قصيدة له غراء. قيل لهم : هذا جهل منكم بمبلغ الفصاحة البشرية وثبوت التفاضل فيها، فإن الفصيح من الشعراء والبليغ من الكتاب والخطباء إنما يباين غيره في بيت أو بيتين من قلائد أشعاره وأبيات قصائده، وكذا الخطيب والكاتب، فأما أن يأتي بكلام في مقدار في دفتر لا يتمكن النحارير العلماء بذلك اللسان من أن يأتوا بمثل سورة قصيرة منها، فليس ذلك بموجود في الطباع، ولا بثابت في المتعارف من العادات وكذا ما وراء القرآن من كلامه عليه السلام وإن كان فصيحا فهو مقدور غيره في الجملة، ولن يباين به غيره الا في ألفاظ قليلة أوتى فيها جوامع الكلم على أن إعطاء مثل ما تدعون له أنتم من الفصاحة تعالى أنه يجعل ذلك علامة لنبوته ودلالة لرسالته دلالة واضحة ومعجزة كافية، والله الهادي إلى الرشاد.
The poets in his brilliant ode. It was said to them: This is ignorance on your part of the extent of human eloquence and the established gradation therein. For the eloquent among poets and the fluent among writers and orators only surpass others in a verse or two from the gems of their poems and the lines of their odes, and likewise the orator and writer. But as for producing speech in the amount of a volume which the masterful scholars of that tongue cannot produce the like of a short sura of it, that is not found in nature, nor is it established in the customary ways. And likewise, other than the Qur'an from his speech, peace be upon him, although it is eloquent, it is within the capability of others in general, and he only surpasses others with it in a few words in which he was given comprehensive speech. But granting the like of what you claim for yourselves of eloquence, He is exalted above that. He makes that a sign for his prophethood and an indication for his message, a clear indication and a sufficient miracle. And Allah guides to the right path.
Source pages p. 756

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the objection that Quranic eloquence is not miraculous because poets and orators can produce eloquent speech. Nasafi argues that the objection stems from ignorance of the true extent of human eloquence and its gradations. He explains that even the most eloquent individuals only surpass others in a verse or two of their entire corpus. In contrast, the Quran presents a continuous discourse of a whole volume where even the most learned experts in the language cannot produce its like in a short sura. This is unprecedented in nature and custom. As for the Prophet's own speech (hadith), though eloquent, it is generally within human capability, differing only in some concise expressions. Thus, attributing such unparalleled eloquence to human capacity is impossible. Allah makes this clear sign a sufficient miracle for prophethood.

Key Terms
فصاحة (eloquence)
إعجاز (inimitability)
معجزة (miracle)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All eloquent speech is equally miraculous; the Quran is just another piece of eloquent Arabic.
Correction: Nasafi distinguishes the sporadic eloquence of humans from the sustained, comprehensive eloquence of the Quran, which is beyond human capacity.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the key difference between the eloquence of poets/orators and the eloquence of the Quran?
A) Poets and orators can produce longer speeches than the Quran.
B) Poets and orators only excel in a few verses, while the Quran's eloquence is sustained throughout a whole sura.
C) The Quran's eloquence is only in its predictions, not in its language.
D) The Prophet's own hadith are equally inimitable.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's unique, sustained eloquence over entire chapters is beyond human capacity, making it a clear sign of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe the Quran is beyond human capacity, why do you still treat it as just another book? What would change in your daily life if you lived with the conviction that every sura is a miracle beyond all human eloquence?

Nasafi distinguishes between the Prophet's human speech and divine revelation. Are you guilty of mixing the two? Take a moment to examine your heart: do you sometimes give hadith the same weight as the Quran without recognizing the difference?
?
The Quran issues a direct challenge to produce something like it. Have you ever felt the weight of that challenge? If you are honest, do you approach the Quran with awe at its impossibility, or have you become numb to its miraculous nature? What is one practical step you can take today to restore that awe?

Three Aspects of the Quran's Miraculous Nature
Nasafi enumerates three aspects of the Quran's miraculous nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational proofs Nasafi offers for the Quran's miraculous nature: knowledge of the unseen, perfect wisdom, and inexhaustible depth.

Core Idea
The Quran's miracle goes beyond eloquence—it reveals knowledge no human could possess.

Nasafi expands on the Quran's miraculous nature by focusing on its content, not just its style. He identifies three specific features that no human could have produced: foreknowledge of future events, perfect wisdom in all rulings, and a depth that exceeds a thousand volumes. This passage invites us to reflect on the divine origin of the Quran through its unique intellectual content.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation once to grasp the overall argument. Notice how Nasafi leads into the three aspects by mentioning other types of evidence.
The passage begins with references to reports of past and future events before focusing on the three core aspects.
2
Identify the three aspects
List the three specific aspects of i'jaz that Nasafi enumerates. Look for the phrases 'الأول... والثاني... والثالث'.
Each aspect is introduced with a distinct reasoning about why it is beyond human capacity.
3
Reflect on each aspect
For each aspect, consider why Nasafi argues it is impossible for a human to produce. Think about the implications of knowledge of the unseen, perfect wisdom, and depth of meaning.
Nasafi emphasizes the illiterate prophet (أمي) and the vast scope of knowledge required.
4
Connect to the overall proof
Understand how these three aspects together point to a divine origin. Nasafi concludes that such a book can only come from the All-Knowing and All-Powerful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبوجه آخر من وجوه دلالات الكتاب ما تضمن من الأخبار في الأمم الماضية، ووجه آخر ما فيه من الإخبار عما يكون في المستقبل، وقد بينا الوجهين. ووجه آخر ما أودع فيه من أصول أحكام النوازل التي تقع إلى قيام الساعة ما بالناس إلى معرفته حاجة، ولن يتصور ذلك إلا من عالم بالغيوب يعلم جميع ما يكون، ويعلم وجه الحكمة والصواب في كل ذلك، ليودع ذلك كله الكتاب، فكان فيه الإعجاز من أوجه ثلاثة: أحدها العلم بما يكون في المستقبل إلى قيام الساعة، وهو علم الغيب لا يعلمه إلا الله تعالى. والثاني: العلم بوجه الحكمة والمصلحة في كل ذلك، وليس في طباع البشر أن يعلم رجل أمي لم ينفق عمره في إحراز العلوم واكتساب الآداب والحكم وجهة الحكمة والصواب والمصلحة في حوادث أسبوع واحد لإنسان واحد من جنس واحد فضلاً عن جميع أجناس الحوادث الواقعة في العبادات، وأنواع المعاملات والمواريث والمعاشرات لجميع العالم إلى آباد الدهر، فعلم أن ذلك ورد من عند علام الغيوب الذي لا يعزب عنه شيء ولا يخفى عليه خافية. والثالث: أنه ليس في مقدور البشر أن يودع في واحد منهم في مقدار دفتر من الكتاب ما يربو من العلوم عند التفتيش والإيضاح والبسط على ألف دفتر وزيادة، فدل أن ذلك بالقادر الذي لا يصعب عليه أمر ولا يعجزه شيء، والله الموفق.
And another aspect of the evidences of the Book is what it contains of reports about past nations, and another aspect is what is in it of reports about what will happen in the future, and we have explained both aspects. And another aspect is that it has deposited in it the principles of rulings of events that occur until the Day of Resurrection, such that people have need of knowledge of them. And that can only be conceived from one who knows the unseen, who knows all that will be, and knows the aspect of wisdom and correctness in all of that, in order to deposit all of that in the Book. So the miraculous nature occurred from three aspects: The first: knowledge of what will be in the future until the Day of Resurrection, and that is knowledge of the unseen, which only Allah knows. The second: knowledge of the aspect of wisdom and benefit in all of that, and it is not in human nature that an illiterate man who has not spent his life acquiring sciences and gaining disciplines and wisdoms should know the aspect of wisdom, correctness, and benefit in the events of one week for one human of one species, let alone all kinds of events occurring in acts of worship, types of transactions, inheritances, and social interactions for all the world until perpetual ages. So it is known that that came from the Knower of the unseen, from whom nothing escapes and no secret is hidden. The third: that it is not within human capability that a single person should deposit in the amount of a volume of the Book that which when examined, clarified, and expanded yields sciences that exceed a thousand volumes and more. So that indicates that it is from the All-Powerful whom no matter is difficult and nothing incapacitates. And Allah is the Giver of success.
Source pages p. 756

Commentary
This passage enumerates three distinct aspects of the Quran's miraculous nature (i'jaz). First, the Quran contains knowledge of future events until the Day of Resurrection, which is knowledge of the unseen exclusive to Allah. Second, the Quran embodies perfect wisdom and benefit in all its rulings and reports — something impossible for an illiterate prophet to devise on his own, as it would require comprehensive knowledge beyond human capacity. Third, the Quran's depth is such that were one to expand and explain the contents of a single volume-like portion, it would yield more than a thousand volumes of knowledge. This indicates that the Quran comes from an all-powerful source. The passage begins by referencing other types of evidences (reports of past and future) but focuses on these three as the core of i'jaz.

Key Terms
إعجاز (inimitability)
علم الغيب (knowledge of the unseen)
حكمة (wisdom)
مصلحة (benefit)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Quran's miracle is only its eloquence.
Correction: Nasafi highlights additional intellectual and prophetic aspects: knowledge of the unseen, perfect wisdom, and depth of knowledge, showing the miracle is multifaceted.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the three aspects of i'jaz mentioned by Nasafi in this passage?
A) Knowledge of future events until the Day of Resurrection.
B) Knowledge of the wisdom and benefit in all rulings.
C) The Quran's ability to cure physical diseases.
D) The impossibility of a human producing such depth of knowledge in a single volume.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's miraculous nature is proven by its foreknowledge, perfect wisdom, and depth—all beyond human capacity.

Nasafi states the obligation to believe in all revealed books.

Belief in all divine books is essential, not just the Qur'an.

Imam Nasafi now turns to the third pillar of faith: belief in Allah's books. This short but important passage establishes that Muslims must affirm all revealed scriptures, not only the Qur'an. The Prophet explicitly mentioned several books, and the obligation is rooted in key Qur'anic verses.

The Wisdom and Obligations of Zakah
Explains the wisdom, rational requirements, and Quranic proofs for zakah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the spiritual, social, and rational dimensions of zakah as presented by Imam al-Nasafi.

Core Idea
Zakah is both a rational duty and a spiritual purification tied to divine wisdom.

Zakah is not merely a financial obligation but an act of worship rooted in deep wisdom. Imam al-Nasafi explains how zakah purifies the giver, benefits society, and aligns with rational requirements. In this passage, he outlines its purposes and supports them with Quranic verses, showing that the full wisdom of its detailed rules is beyond human grasp.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the flow from general wisdom to specific rational conditions.
Pay attention to the Quranic verses cited at the end.
2
Identify the key purposes of zakah
The opening states that zakah purifies the giver and brings praise. Also, it provides assistance to the weak—the greatest social interest.
Look for the phrase 'أعظم وجوه المصالح'.
3
List the rational requirements
The passage says 'ثم العقل يقتضي...'. Find the four requirements: giving what is good, willingly, expecting reward only from God, and not reproaching.
These are explicit in the text.
4
Match verses to requirements
The author cites five Quranic verses. Match each to the corresponding point: spending from good (2:267), seeking Allah's pleasure (2:265), condemning laziness (9:54), forbidding nullification by reproach (2:264), and purification (92:18).
This shows the harmony between reason and revelation.
5
Reflect on the concluding remark
The passage ends by saying the full wisdom of zakah’s details is beyond human comprehension. This humbles the believer.
Consider why this is important for a theological worldview.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانيا : الزكاة عبادة وأما الزكاة فقد ورد بها النبي عليه السلام على ما تقتضيه الحكمة، إذ هي تزكي صاحبها وتثمر له الحمد والثناء، وفي إيجابها أعظم وجوه المصالح، وهو المعونة للضعفاء، ولا مصلحة أعم من أن يظهر القوى للضعيف حسن المعونة على تسوية حاله وأمر معاشه مع ما فيه من شكر الله تعالى على ما اختصه به من السعة، ورياضة النفس على أداء الأمانات، والتبرؤ من الشح والتمسح لأبواب المصالح، إذا النفس مجبولة على الضن بالمال وشرف الإنسان مقرون بإفاضة الجود على وجوه الخيرات، ثم العقل يقتضي أن يتقرب العبد إلى خالقه بأداء ما هو الطيب دون الخبيث، وأن يتسارع إلى أداء ذلك بطيب نفس منه دون الكراهية والكسل، وأن لا يتوقع به الجزاء إلا من الله تعالى إذ هو يتقرب إليه ولا يمن على المعطي بما فعل، فورد ما بلغه محمد عليه السلام من الكتاب بذلك كله قال في الأول: يَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا أَنفِقُوا مِن طَيِّبَتِ مَا كَسَبْتُمْ وقال في الثاني: الَّذِينَ يُنفِقُونَ أَمْوَالَهُمُ ابْتِغاءَ مَرْضَاتِ اللَّهِ وَتَلْبِينَا مِنْ أَنفُسِهِمْ وقال في ذم من يضاد هذه الحالة: وَلَا يَأْتُونَ الصَّلَوَة إِلَّا وَهُمْ كُسَالَى وَلَا يُنفِقُونَ إِلَّا وَهُمْ كَرِهُونَ ثم قال في الثالث: لَا تُبْطِلُوا صَدَقَتِكُم بِالْمَنْ وَالْأَذَى وقال: يُؤْتِي مَالَهُ يَتَزَكَّى يبين أصناف الأموال وما يجب في كل صنف، وأصناف من يجب الصرف إليهم على وجه لو استغرق الحكيم عمره بالتأمل ليقف على كنه ما في ذلك من الحكمة لما وقف عليه، والله الموفق.
Second: Zakah — an act of worship. As for zakah, the Prophet, peace be upon him, brought it according to what wisdom requires, for it purifies its giver and yields for him praise and commendation. In its obligation are the greatest aspects of interests, which is assistance for the weak. And there is no interest more general than that the strong shows good assistance to the weak in settling his situation and his livelihood, along with gratitude to God Almighty for what He has favored him with of abundance, and training the soul to fulfill trusts, and disassociating from stinginess, and cleansing the doors of interests, for the soul is disposed to be miserly with wealth, and the honor of a person is connected to the outpouring of generosity upon the faces of good deeds. Then reason requires that the servant draw near to his Creator by giving what is good, not what is vile, and to hasten to do that with a willing soul without aversion or laziness, and not to expect recompense from anyone except God Almighty, for he is drawing near to Him, and not to reproach the recipient for his action. So what Muhammad, peace be upon him, conveyed from the Book came with all of that. He said in the first: "O you who believe, spend from the good things you have earned" [Quran 2:267]. And He said in the second: "Those who spend their wealth seeking the pleasure of Allah and affirming [their faith] from themselves" [Quran 2:265]. And He said in condemnation of those who oppose this state: "And they do not come to prayer except while they are lazy, and they do not spend except while they are averse" [Quran 9:54]. Then He said in the third: "Do not nullify your charities by reproach and harm" [Quran 2:264]. And He said: "He who gives his wealth to purify himself" [Quran 92:18]. He explains the categories of wealth and what is obligatory in each category, and the categories of those to whom it must be given, such that if a wise man spent his entire life in reflection to grasp the essence of the wisdom in that, he would not grasp it. And God is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 770

Commentary
This passage defines zakah as an act of worship and explains its wisdom. The author begins by stating that the Prophet brought zakah according to wisdom (hikma). Its primary benefit is that it purifies the giver (tuzakki sahibaha) and brings him praise from God and people. The greatest social interest (maslaha) in its obligation is assistance to the weak. The author then elaborates: there is no more universal interest than the strong helping the weak to improve their situation, combined with gratitude to God for His blessings, training the soul to fulfill trusts, and shedding miserliness. The human soul is naturally stingy, but human honor is linked to generosity. Reason ('aql) then imposes certain conditions: the believer must give from what is good (tayyib), not bad; must do so willingly without aversion or laziness; must expect reward only from God; and must not reproach the recipient. After presenting these rational arguments, the author cites Quranic verses to substantiate each point: spending from good things (2:267), spending seeking God's pleasure (2:265), condemning laziness and aversion (9:54), forbidding nullification by reproach (2:264), and the one who gives to purify himself (92:18). The passage concludes that the complete wisdom of the detailed rules of zakah (categories of wealth and recipients) is beyond human comprehension, even if one devoted a lifetime to understanding it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Zakah is merely a tax or financial obligation without spiritual significance.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that zakah is an act of worship that purifies the giver, yields praise, and fulfills rational and spiritual demands, not just a financial duty.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a rational requirement for giving zakah?
A) Giving the best and purest of one's wealth
B) Giving with a willing heart without laziness
C) Expecting reward from the recipient's gratitude
D) Not reproaching the recipient after giving

Key Takeaway
Zakah combines spiritual purification, social welfare, and rational duty, all rooted in divine wisdom and confirmed by the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you give charity, do you sometimes give what you no longer want? The passage demands giving from the best. How does that challenge your practice? What will you change this week?
?
Do you ever feel hesitant or lazy about paying zakah? The passage says reason requires giving with a willing soul without aversion. Reflect on any reluctance in your heart. What does it reveal about your love for Allah?
?
Have you ever felt superior or looked down on someone after giving them charity? The passage warns against nullifying charity by reproach. How will you guard your heart from pride the next time you give?
